## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Produce answer.json** — Write ALL output to `/workspace/answer.json` with this structure:
   ```json
   {
     "analysis": {
       "summary": "Brief description of your approach",
       "files_examined": [{"path": "file.ext", "description": "..."}],
       "reasoning": "Detailed explanation or analysis"
     },
     "changes": [
       {"file": "path.ext", "description": "...", "diff": "unified diff"}
     ]
   }
   ```
   Omit `changes` if the task is analysis-only. Do NOT edit source files directly — produce diffs in `changes[]` instead.

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Rust-Servo Shared Style System Discovery

## Your Task

The Rust compiler and Servo browser engine share code via common Rust crates. Find: 1. In `servo/servo`: the Cargo.toml files under `components/style/` and `components/selectors/` that define the `style` and `selectors` crates — report each crate's declared dependencies. 2. In `servo/servo`: the main entry point file for the style system (`components/style/lib.rs`). 3. In `rust-lang/rust`: find if any crate under `compiler/` or `library/` depends on or shares code with Servo's `selectors` crate (search for `selectors` in Cargo.toml files). 4. In `rust-lang/rust`: the file that defines the `proc_macro` bridge which Servo build scripts use. Report each file path and the key dependency or symbol.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out. Use Sourcegraph MCP tools to explore the codebase.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7` (rust-lang/rust)
- `sg-evals/servo--be6a2f99` (servo/servo)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

72-assistanttext-
I've completed a comprehensive discovery of the Rust-Servo shared style system. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Discoveries

**1. Servo's Style System Architecture**
- Servo does **NOT** have `components/style/` or `components/selectors/` directories
- Instead, Servo depends on an external **Stylo repository** (https://github.com/servo/stylo)
- In Servo's root `Cargo.toml`: both `selectors` and `stylo` are imported from the Stylo git repository at revision `3b46f3ef27eb14ca276b4bf3ff041a6c43d93827`

**2. Servo Components Using Selectors**
Found 4 crates that depend on the `selectors` crate:
- `components/layout/Cargo.toml` (line 49)
- `components/script/Cargo.toml` (line 129)
- `components/shared/layout/Cargo.toml` (line 35)
- `tests/unit/style/Cargo.toml` (line 22)

**3. Rust-Servo Connection**
The Rust compiler's `src/tools/cargotest/main.rs` includes Servo as a test target, specifically testing the `selectors` package. This ensures Rust's compiler is compatible with Servo/Stylo's CSS selector implementation.

**4. Proc_macro Bridge Definition**
The proc_macro bridge (used by Servo build scripts) is defined in Rust's standard library:
- **Main file**: `library/proc_macro/src/bridge/mod.rs`
- **Key structure**: `BridgeConfig<'a>` (line 154)
  - Establishes active connection between proc_macro client and server
  - Contains buffer for input, dispatch closure for RPC, and panic hook control
  - Explicitly implements `!Send` and `!Sync` for safety
- **Supporting files**: 
  - `library/proc_macro/src/bridge/server.rs` - Server-side implementation
  - `library/proc_macro/src/bridge/client.rs` - Client-side implementation

All findings have been documented in `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, relevant symbols, and detailed analysis.

    "content": "1: //! Internal interface for communicating between a `proc_macro` client\n2: //! (a proc macro crate) and a `proc_macro` server (a compiler front-end).\n3: //!\n4: //! Serialization (with C ABI buffers) and unique integer handles are employed\n5: //! to allow safely interfacing between two copies of `proc_macro` built\n6: //! (from the same source) by different compilers with potentially mismatching\n7: //! Rust ABIs (e.g., stage0/bin/rustc vs stage1/bin/rustc during bootstrap).\n8: \n9: #![deny(unsafe_code)]\n10: \n11: use std::hash::Hash;\n12: use std::ops::{Bound, Range};\n13: use std::sync::Once;\n14: use std::{fmt, marker, mem, panic, thread};\n15: \n16: use crate::{Delimiter, Level, Spacing};\n17: \n18: /// Higher-order macro describing the server RPC API, allowing automatic\n19: /// generation of type-safe Rust APIs, both client-side and server-side.\n20: ///\n21: /// `with_api!(MySelf, my_self, my_macro)` expands to:\n22: /// ```rust,ignore (pseudo-code)\n23: /// my_macro! {\n24: ///     // ...\n25: ///     Literal {\n26: ///         // ...\n27: ///         fn character(ch: char) -> MySelf::Literal;\n28: ///         // ...\n29: ///         fn span(my_self: &MySelf::Literal) -> MySelf::Span;\n30: ///         fn set_span(my_self: &mut MySelf::Literal, span: MySelf::Span);\n31: ///     },\n32: ///     // ...\n33: /// }\n34: /// ```\n35: ///\n36: /// The first two arguments serve to customize the arguments names\n37: /// and argument/return types, to enable several different usecases:\n38: ///\n39: /// If `my_self` is just `self`, then each `fn` signature can be used\n40: /// as-is for a method. If it's anything else (`self_` in practice),\n41: /// then the signatures don't have a special `self` argument, and\n42: /// can, therefore, have a different one introduced.\n43: ///\n44: /// If `MySelf` is just `Self`, then the types are only valid inside\n45: /// a trait or a trait impl, where the trait has associated types\n46: /// for each of the API types. If non-associated types are desired,\n47: /// a module name (`self` in practice) can be used instead of `Self`.\n48: macro_rules! with_api {\n49:     ($S:ident, $self:ident, $m:ident) => {\n50: track_env_var(var: &str, value: Option<&str>);\n55:                 fn track_path(path: &str);\n56:                 fn literal_from_str(s: &str) -> Result<Literal<$S::Span, $S::Symbol>, ()>;\n57:                 fn emit_diagnostic(diagnostic: Diagnostic<$S::Span>);\n58:             },\n59:             TokenStream {\n60:                 fn drop($self: $S::TokenStream);\n61:                 fn    base: Option<$S::TokenStream>,\n71:                     trees: Vec<TokenTree<$S::TokenStream, $S::Span, $S::Symbol>>,\n72:                 ) -> $S::TokenStream;\n73:                 fn The other `Delimiter` variants should be used\n803:     /// instead in this context. This is a rustc bug. \"1.29.0\")]\n926: pub enum Spacing {\n927:     /// A `Punct` token can join with the following token to form a multi-character operator.\n928:     ///\n929:     /// In token streams constructed using proc macro interfaces, `Joint` punctuation tokens can be\n930:     /// followed by any other tokens. However, in token streams parsed from source code, the\n931:     /// compiler will only set spacing to `Joint` in the following cases.\n932:     /// - When a `Punct` is immediately followed by another `Punct` without a whitespace. E.g. `+`\n933:     ///   is `Joint` in `+=` and `++`.\n934:     /// - When a single quote `'` is immediately followed by an identifier without a whitespace.\n935:     ///   E.g. `'` is `Joint` in `'lifetime`.\n936:     ///\n937:     /// This list may be extended in the future to enable more token combinations.\n938:     #[stable(feature = \"proc_macro_lib2\", since = \"1.29.0\")]\n939:     Joint,\n940:     /// A `Punct` token cannot join with the following token to form a multi-character operator.\n941:     ///\n942:     /// `Alone` punctuation tokens can be followed by any other tokens. In token streams parsed\n943:     /// from source code, the compiler will set spacing to `Alone` in all cases not covered by the\n944:     /// conditions for `Joint` above. E.g. `+` is `Alone` in `+ =`, `+ident` and `+()`. In\n945:     /// particular, tokens not followed by anything will be marked as `Alone`.\n946:     #[stable(feature = \"proc_macro_lib2\", since = \"1.29.0\")]\n947:     Alone,\n948: }\n949: \n950:
